  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47f34e3e-1486-4847-ac1c-54cf804dc9a7'

<div id="review_293102420" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293102420" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293102420?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781417687053" href="/book/show/7666936-silver-is-for-secrets">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jenn by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4189131-holly-noelle">Holly Noelle</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=withcraft-and-wizardry">withcraft-and-wizardry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=annoying-protagonist">annoying-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=2-star-reads">2-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293102420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12966625933957839014">...<br/><br/>What the hell just happened here?<br/><br/>I honestly don't even know how I feel about this book. Literally every character in this book pissed me off at one point. Actually, the only one who I could stand at the end was Jacob. Everything about this plot had me frustrated. How - after 2 years of this - Stacey's friends still question her nightmares. It's like, wake the fuck up! She saved your asses before, have some god damn faith!<br/><br/>And Stacey, come on! Grow a god damn backbone and speak up. For a main c</span>
  <span id="freeText12966625933957839014" style="display:none">...<br /><br />What the hell just happened here?<br /><br />I honestly don't even know how I feel about this book. Literally every character in this book pissed me off at one point. Actually, the only one who I could stand at the end was Jacob. Everything about this plot had me frustrated. How - after 2 years of this - Stacey's friends still question her nightmares. It's like, wake the fuck up! She saved your asses before, have some god damn faith!<br /><br />And Stacey, come on! Grow a god damn backbone and speak up. For a main character, there's just not enough presence - nothing that comes from her. I find her extremely weak. But weirdly, I don't blame the character, I blame the writer. Stolarz, to me, seems like she's writing what she thinks teenagers/young adults are like and then taking it twelve steps farther and writing that down. Nothing about these friendships is believable. Nothing about their day-to-day lives are believable. And if you want me to care about your characters, don't make them so god damn stupid and annoying. Case in point: Clara.<br /><br />Clara has to be the worst written character ever in a book. This is a combination of character and writing. If we were supposed to care that she was in danger - well, epic fail there. I cringed every time she came around.<br /><br />I will say that the epilogue was my favorite part. The fact that it was an entire chapter written from journals, transcripts, and news articles was interesting and actually good. Too bad the entire book wasn't written like this.<br /><br />I will go onto the next one and I will hold on to the bright light that is Jacob. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12966625933957839014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15104554044082167453">I have been enjoying this YA paranormal series lately; it has been on my TBR list for awhile and I thought it would be cute to read it on Remembrance Day for NO REASON other than the title, Red is for Remembrance.   <span id="freeText15104554044082167453" style="display:none">I have been enjoying this YA paranormal series lately; it has been on my TBR list for awhile and I thought it would be cute to read it on Remembrance Day for NO REASON other than the title, Red is for Remembrance. I really love that it is representing Stacy as a young, psychic Wiccan, which really is no more than a natural talent for herbs, healing and respect for the earth. In this book we find Stacey and her closest friends from her boarding school, like Drea and Amber, and their boyfriends, all looking forward to a perfect vacation before they start college.<br />Friends, a cottage on the beach, and no parents... It all goes perfectly until her nightmares return, this time about Clara, a girl in another cottage, and it's about her death. Stacey can't figure out her dreams in time, and with horrific consequences; a tragedy that will forever haunt her.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2914272743" />
    <a title="Trisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1238273-trisha"><img alt="Trisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600736566p2/1238273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2914272743?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha" href="/user/show/1238273-trisha">Trisha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2914272743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10396412612264470128"><i>"Keeping secrets doesn't bring people together, it only pulls them apart."</i><br/><br/>Stacey's off on a vacation with her friends - the same roommates she's already had - and their significant others. They want to have fun and hang out again together. But soon into the holiday, Stacey has new symptoms and nightmares and she knows someone is in danger.<br/><br/>I think my biggest frustration with this one is it felt like a lot of repeated stuff. We kept having to deal with Clara, over and over again. It was frustratin</span>
  <span id="freeText10396412612264470128" style="display:none"><i>"Keeping secrets doesn't bring people together, it only pulls them apart."</i><br /><br />Stacey's off on a vacation with her friends - the same roommates she's already had - and their significant others. They want to have fun and hang out again together. But soon into the holiday, Stacey has new symptoms and nightmares and she knows someone is in danger.<br /><br />I think my biggest frustration with this one is it felt like a lot of repeated stuff. We kept having to deal with Clara, over and over again. It was frustrating that, again, no one really talked. Stacey downplayed what she was going through but then also went over the top with it (like running off into strange houses on her own). It seemed like everyone was keeping secrets and no one was communicating and we just had to keep reading again Clara butting in everywhere. It made what should have been a fun book annoying. I wish I'd liked it more. <br /><br />Also, I'm sad at the conclusion of this one. I'm sure there can't be a quick answer other than the obvious one so I'm curious to see where the next story takes us.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10396412612264470128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

As Clara tried to hurt Stacey , they are interrupted momentarilly by Jacob .   <span id="freeText7977368078386858758" style="display:none">Last 20 pages: 4 stars. Rest of the book: 2.5 stars. My main complaint: WHY ARE THERE NO LIKABLE CHARACTERS IN THIS SERIES?! Seriously. There is one like-able character, and he was barely in this book. <br /><br />Our protagonist, Stacey, is spineless and has no personality - hasn't throughout the entire series. I this that has been what is missing from this book series, and why I can't give any of these books a higher rating than 2.5 stars. <br /><br />And this book in particular was difficult because the innocent that Stacey was trying to save was SO unlikable (though we understand why later). All in all, it's hard to relate to anyone in this series. <br /><br />I appreciated that this book was a <i>tad</i> les predictable than its predecessors. Like I said, last 20 pages = 4 stars. I appreciated the way that the epilogue was put together, too. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong - the series is entertaining, and it's easy to zip through the books. I'm just enjoying them less than I did when I was 16. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12686488359097116989">Where to begin?? Clara's character: from the very beginning I was kind of wishing that maybe Stacey would see all the damage she was doing and just pack up and leave town. I don't think she is a character ANYONE could sympathize with. But you have to admit that Donovan was right...she can't keep her nose out of everyone's business and it eventually turns around to bite you on the rear! HOWEVER, I CANNOT believe that Jacob is gone!!!!! I bawled my eyes out over that one. He was having nightmares </span>
  <span id="freeText12686488359097116989" style="display:none">Where to begin?? Clara's character: from the very beginning I was kind of wishing that maybe Stacey would see all the damage she was doing and just pack up and leave town. I don't think she is a character ANYONE could sympathize with. But you have to admit that Donovan was right...she can't keep her nose out of everyone's business and it eventually turns around to bite you on the rear! HOWEVER, I CANNOT believe that Jacob is gone!!!!! I bawled my eyes out over that one. He was having nightmares of his own death and withheld that information because of his love for Stacey and wanting to help her and protect her. So sad. I have a love/hate for books that are like this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12686488359097116989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2378557616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2378557616" />
    <a title="Brooklyn Betts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59409846-brooklyn-betts"><img alt="Brooklyn Betts" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2378557616?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooklyn Betts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooklyn Betts" href="/user/show/59409846-brooklyn-betts">Brooklyn Betts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2378557616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11076440617481813834">The book "Silver is for Secrets" was written by Laurie Faria Stolarz. It is about a girl named Stacey who went to a beach cottage with her friends and boyfriend to try and have a relaxing summer. However, she starts to have nightmares again that allow he to see into the future, and she needs to save someone else now. Clara, the girl she assumes she needs to save, is giving Stacey and her friends a hard time. Stacey seems to be the only one who wants to help save her life, which really stresses S</span>
  <span id="freeText11076440617481813834" style="display:none">The book "Silver is for Secrets" was written by Laurie Faria Stolarz. It is about a girl named Stacey who went to a beach cottage with her friends and boyfriend to try and have a relaxing summer. However, she starts to have nightmares again that allow he to see into the future, and she needs to save someone else now. Clara, the girl she assumes she needs to save, is giving Stacey and her friends a hard time. Stacey seems to be the only one who wants to help save her life, which really stresses Stacey out. Her boyfriend, Jacob is keeping secrets from her, and she starts to lose trust in him. Little does she know something tragic is going to happen that will change her life forever.<br /><br />In my opinion, I really liked this book. It was very mysterious, and kept me on my toes. When I thought one thing was definitely going to happen, something completely different did instead. I like how all of the characters are very different, and have distinct personalities. It gave the book a very interesting touch that I really enjoyed. I also liked how at some points you didn't know what was going to happen until it did happen, and at other points you could figure out what was going to happen along with the characters. I didn't really like how the ending was very out of nowhere, and just happened all of a sudden. I feel like there should have been more content to lead up to the ending. Other than that, I thought it was a very good book, and I can't wait to read the next one.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to people who enjoy mystery, magic and who like to read things that are relatable. A lot of teenagers would probably enjoy this book because the story is based on the lives of teenagers and all of the problems they have. This book is definitely for older audiences because it has more mature parts to it that may not be appropriate for younger children. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11076440617481813834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970677082" />
    <a title="Trinity" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64054056-trinity"><img alt="Trinity" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494272384p2/64054056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970677082?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trinity" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trinity" href="/user/show/64054056-trinity">Trinity</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970677082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12980091806071943538">Laurie Stolarz’s Silver is for Secrets, is exciting and engaging. It’s the third book in the series, but it’s just as charming as the first, if not a bit more because of the change of setting. The style is pretty much the same throughout all the books, which I like.<br/>	 Stacey has become more paranoid, with new mysteries to solve and premonitions to decode. Clara is a new character, she’s the one Stacey’s having premonitions about this time. She seems really sweet and innocent, then she starts flir</span>
  <span id="freeText12980091806071943538" style="display:none">Laurie Stolarz’s Silver is for Secrets, is exciting and engaging. It’s the third book in the series, but it’s just as charming as the first, if not a bit more because of the change of setting. The style is pretty much the same throughout all the books, which I like.<br />	 Stacey has become more paranoid, with new mysteries to solve and premonitions to decode. Clara is a new character, she’s the one Stacey’s having premonitions about this time. She seems really sweet and innocent, then she starts flirting with Chad and PJ, which makes Drea and Amber really mad. Stacey still really wants to help her. She seems to be hiding something though. <br />	Amber wasn’t very important in the first two books; she did help, but not that much. However she’s much more important in this book. Jacob seems to be the perfect boyfriend. He’s really nice and sweet, and that would be great, if he wasn’t keeping a secret. Stacey is really worried about this secret and is mad he wont tell her about it. <br />	In the first book the threats are centered on Drea, and in the second book Stacey, in this book everything is centered on Clara. Though Clara annoys Stacey and her friends Stacey doesn’t want to let her die. The seaside setting allows for more room to work the plot and shady characters in, making it hard to find out whom the bad guy is. Even with all this going on, the plot twist at the end is unpredictable.<br />	Though it’s the third book it keeps you interested. I suggest this book if you liked the first two or if you like witchcraft, with a side of mystery and romance. If you haven’t read Blue is for Nightmare, or White is for Magic, I suggest you read them too.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

She's getting better at using her magic, better at listening and acting on the magic. Jacob was a good help for that. Fucking Chad. That bastard just can't stop kissing other girls. I get that Drea "loves" him but the asshole thought he loved Stacey and then made out with some random girl. That is not love. Drea is still a fucking brat and the surprise crazy bitch at the end was insane. <br /><br />And not in the fucking good way. <br /><br />I mean, it was the stupidest plot twist. It's also the same plot twist that the other two books used as well. So... what's the next book's twist going to be? If who's dead is really dead I WILL BE PISSED. he was the only positive thing in this whole fucking series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13646153625332615442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

All of the books in this series are exactly the same.   <span id="freeText14894689469480411452" style="display:none">0.25<br />This book was so exhausting to read that I had to mentally push myself to read like 20 pages at a time. All of the books in this series are exactly the same. Stacey has a nightmare, her friends don't believe her, Stacey does some random "spell" stuff that doesn't actually do anything, drama drama drama, and then the books end with some abrupt ending where the bad guy gets revealed and someone dies. So tired of it. I'm glad that I'm almost done with the series, but I'm honestly dreading reading the next book.</span>

This series follows Stacey Brown, a young Wiccan with psychic powers. Stacey learns to use her abilities in order to investigate crimes, missing persons, and complications that come up in her daily life. As the series evolves Stacey graduates from high school, learns how to better harness her abilities, and sorts through her complicated love life.<br/><br/>-Miss Emily</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OME5BwE5B0X8n7ut8zxAMABkX0/UBC3pmqZOKicXVZ/ifskoUxbcUwRoS7t7MwouH3fnPEGU/TiRcKUK88ufGg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vUvVxnPnFAdeYdujSJma/+A7T03BqKnMXb6dwEtBxm9n9CXpIcjPEaaWK7XAltDh/yj3PlQ4eR1WaHbgn50M6g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9346778473436416691">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br/><br/>Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br/><br/>Stolarz found sales success with he</span>
  <span id="freeText9346778473436416691" style="display:none">Laurie Faria Stolarz grew up in Salem, MA, attended Merrimack College, and received an MFA in Creative Writing from Emerson College in Boston. <br /><br />Laurie Faria Stolarz is an American author of young adult fiction novels, best known for her Blue is for Nightmares series. Her works, which feature teenage protagonists, blend elements found in mystery and romance novels.<br /><br />Stolarz found sales success with her first novel, Blue is for Nightmares, and followed it up with three more titles in the series, White is for Magic, Silver is for Secrets, and Red is for Remembrance, as well as a companion graphic novel, Black is for Beginnings. Stolarz is also the author of the Touch series (Deadly Little Secret, Deadly Little Lies, Deadly Little Games, Deadly Little Voices, and Deadly Little Lessons), as well as Bleed and Project 17. With more than two million books sold worldwide, Stolarz's titles have been named on various awards list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9346778473436416691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
